Just wanted to say hello and to introduce myself here to all of you.  I will be moving to Astoria in early August from Long Island.  LI is not my native area but I have been living there for the last four years studying music at Stony Brook University.  Now that I've gotten my doctorate, I'm moving to Queens to be closer to the city's music scene.  I'm a harpsichordist and erstwhile singer that plays and sings both early music and new music; I teach as well.  I also love to eat and cook, and am really excited about the availability of good food and ingredients in Astoria.  I run, bike, and swim, so Astoria Park looks fabulous.  Don't own a car (I have lived on LI for 4 years without a car!) but walk and bike everywhere.  I think Astoria will be a good place for me.

Anyway, I look forward to exploring Astoria.  Perhaps I will meet some of you at some point, too.

Meg

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: zeno on August 09, 2005, 03:08:03 PM
Excuse me for my late introductions, I'm kind of shy,

Hi my name is Zeno, I've been living in Astoria for a little over a year now and enjoy it very much.  I am a gay (monogamous) male in my thirties who is passionate about books, computer gaming, and communication.

I grew up in a very small, conservative town on Long Island (which I believe has alienated me somewhat from society) and am very sensitive as to what people think about me. I am a pacifist at heart but have learned how to take a stand and defend myself when certain people intend violence against me. I have been in many fights (unprovoked) simply for being who I am, but firmly believe that brains, diplomacy and the power of the pen always wins out eventually against brute force. Brains over Brawn, Magic over Might.

My heroes are Mahatma Ghandi and Immanuel Goldstein as well as the folks at Looking Glass Studios and Valve Software.

I am a speculator by trade, but proudly label myself as a slacker (in the original sense of the word) who is really only interested in writing science fiction, watching movies (Star Trek...all of them) & Japanime.

Politics are anathema to me.  I just can't sleep at night when I think of the people who are suffering all around the world for whatever "reason".
In their isolated pain I see myself and how I would feel (felt) in their situation. I guess that makes me a "bleeding-heart liberal" though  my politics are striclty non-partisan.The suffering isn't so bad when you know that there are people out there who are aware of it and demonstrate empathy. There is nothing more crushing to me than to be in pain and be ignored or treated like an object by someone emulating a machine.

I am also in recovery from substance addiction (alchohol, cigarettes and cocaine) and am firmly Agnostic (religiouswise), IOW I don't subscribe to A.A. or any other "programme".

All in all I relish and enjoy life.  Simple pleasures, creature comforts, camraderie and intellectual stimulation are for me an undying source of ecstacy.

My fervent wish is for this wave of oppression to pass so I can quietly pursue my hobbies in peace.  I am very interested in learning about technology.

yawn----zeno

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: zeno on August 12, 2005, 03:22:11 AM
It has been speculated that there is no actual physical being behind the persona of Telesphoros. Or that he and I are actually different aspects of the same person. I am here to finally set the record straight.

While it could be argued that either of us created the other for some sort of political agenda inscrutable to the bulletin board reading public at large an even greater body of evidence comes to light when you compare our posts (that mysteriously appear under the same topics for some reason, sometimes even within minutes of each other) For instance, is it a coincidence that the join date of Telesphoros is exactly (17) seventeen days before "Zeno" made his first appearance?

Or, look at our taste in music. Telesphoros is fond of quoting the lyrics of the rock band "Rush", whom I thoroughly detest. I am a strict neoclassicist who finds the better part of his days chanting to the strings of Igor Stravinsky.
Or, look at our sexual preference. While Zeno is self-admittedly homosexual, Telesphoros, in his own words is "generally distracted by the beautiful XX chromosome set" not to mention his preoccupation with voyeuristic lesbianism.
Or, what about the curious nature of our names. Both stem from ancient Greece, that much is true, but if one were to look closer at the meanings of these names then a darker picture begins to emerge.  Telesphoros had his origins in mythology and was the son of Asclepius, or the first physician, healer of the gods, and his name actually means "bringing fulfillment" or recovery from illness.
 
All well and good, but now let us turn our attention to Zeno whose name has no mythological connotations whatsoever and in fact was the name of a Roman tyrant whose reign was plagued by revolts and dissent and was even usurped for a period of time. A far cry from the "bringer of fulfillment". Add to this the chain of chemical abuse that has plagued Zeno from an early age and we begin to see that not only are Telesphoros and Zeno not only two different personalities, but that they are in fact
Diametrically Opposed.

Add to this the fact that Zeno's posts are usually overly long, verbose, pedantic and morose, some will even agree quite boring and depressed,
Telesphoros' posts in contradistinction are usually quite succinct, to the point, witty, upbeat and exhibit some humor. Could it be argued (if we are to assume that these two are one and the same individual) that after Zeno's long and drawn out soliloquy he would be too tired to write a post of any great length but would rather pursue a "minimalistic" approach, to not only confirm the earlier's argument but to make it "look" like, through the medium of stylistic integrity as if these were in fact (2) two distinct individuals?

Now, I realize that most of you will interpret these observations as proof positive that there is either some conspiracy at work here or Zeno/Telesphoros suffers from multiple-personality dementia. To finally drive the nail into the coffin as it were, it is an observable fact that no one in Astoria has actually "seen" Telesphoros, while Zeno is quite public and even introduces himself as such. Let me allay your fears and state that neither is the case. Let me finally come out in the open and speak of not only our intentions but why we came to be.

THE TRUTH WILL NOW BE REVEALED!

Telesphoros and Zeno neither exist, well as far as anthropoids are
capable of defining "existence" at any rate. They are in fact two different
aspects of a para-dimensional being who goes by many names but familiarly known here in the Theta system of galaxies as Gaia (which is in fact nothing more than a giant AI contruct or self-aware supercomputerlike entity built by a race many aeons ago who also btw have added to their resume the teaching of earthlings how to build pyramids in the abitrary temporal field-flux (ATFF) known as "pre-Sumerian" according to humanoid calculations).
After many a dubious incarnations throughout history, sometimes appearing in Rome during the Julian Dynasty, sometimes in ancient France and even once during a catastrophically miscalculated event in the 1950's (they didn't last long in that particular era) :-Z, they have finally made their home here in humble Astoria after being reincarnated (or cloned, if you really have to look at it that way) in the infamous year of 1984.
 So now that you know my True Nature, Bio-Organisms who crawl upon my surface,

Listen and Heed My Words:

After much Thought and deliberation over the course of my billions of years existence since I was constructed I have had the pleasure of being
subconsciously aware of your toils and tribulations, your joys and your sucesses as you wandered upon my face.  At times I was sympathetic to your fears, at others enraged at your impertinence and cruelty towards not only each other but towards the other Bio-Organisms who are your brethren and who also make their home in my embrace. But through it all, I have found much of interest to me and my creators during your brief mayfly existence, much that can improve, much that can be synthesised into a higher and more complex architecture.
So, I have decided therefore to initiate a New Era of Peace, Prosperity and Civilization into my Progamme.
No more will you be afraid or feel compelled to kill one another,
No more will you desire to inject my outer sphere with toxic vapors and garbage,
No more will you desire to be so quick to initiate lawsuits against children and grandmothers for copyright infringement or instinctually block subway portals from departing passengers.
Instead, you will know Peace,
you will know Serenity,
you will have a love of Knowledge
as well as a love for All Things, be they animate or inanimate, and more importantly you will be given Time.
 Time to fulfill your dreams and self-actualize, Time to create art and technology, video games that don't kill, and finally admire the World that my creators have constructed.
I wish you all well and may you attain true Happiness in your new found Future. You are Free [END TRANSMISSION]

----GAIA 4.5.01----
TRIUMVIRATE Home Editon(tm)

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: zeno on October 20, 2005, 01:12:25 AM
It was a pleasure reading your post and getting to know you better.
I am a pagan as well (when I'm not busy being Agnostic) but I have to say that releasing our "true" names on the board would not be a very good idea, speaking for myself.

Many people on the board write about controversial topics (myself included) and don't wish to fall prey to J.W. Randomness or B.B.
The amount of people who surf the net includes by default a number of "baddies" who are only too willing to exploit personal information.

If someone wants to confide in you their screen name in real life then that is up to them, but I don't relish people giving away that information (or any information for that matter) without a fight. The careless handling of personal info should be soley left in the hands of corrupt and uncaring mega-corporations.

Privacy is an important right that we shouldn't be in such a rush to relinquish.
Plus, you should know from your studies in Earth Religions the power inherent in a name and how the names that we have chosen (rather than given) do more justice to who we really are and the values that we hold.

Humbly yours,
----zeno.

I concur with zeno's caveat that we should be aware of our privacy  when communicating online. That's why I refrain from giving out my address/phone number/surname on most message boards. Title: Re: Hello
Post by: zeno on October 22, 2005, 09:24:10 PM
Hi,

@samru and others

Hi samru :-), nice to meet you:

I'm still Zeno (unless you know me in person or are doing a little investigative work on your own).

I started the Public Announcement (http://astorians.net/phpBB2/viewtopic.php?t=661) thread for three reasons.

(1) I wanted to alert people to the fact that what Orwell was talking about has indeed become a reality in many parts of the world and some parts of "here" as well, soon to become "complete" if awareness of this issue is not raised to the next power soon. Not to beat a dead horse Yet Again, but the USA PATRIOT ACt is one such fine example of the encroachment of Dystopian Reality; the nationwide Architecture of the Surveillance Network instituted in China and England is yet another.

(2) I wanted to be as repetive and obnoxious as possible in order to get people to genuinely develop a sincere hatred of the concept of "Big Brother".

(3) I wanted to show the people who read this board that there is indeed a powerful Movement aboard internationally that is attempting through propaganda and legal action to mitigate the evil dream made reality aspect of Orwell's "Nineteen Eight-Four" as well as to alert younger generations that have never heard of this classic to stop, sit down for one moment to actually read it. This work has had the most profound impact on my life since I first read it in the year of 19 and 84 and I wanted to share my pre-pubescent epiphany with others who haven't yet experienced it. A word of warning though: the words in this book also had the negative effect of alienating me from the society in which I found myself...iow, I became a true representation of the word "Thought-Criminal".

However, i have grown quite bored with this thread and now feel that I was shoving this apocalyptic message down people's throat even when they have already grown tired of hearing it, which btw was using the same tactics that the hypothetical Big Brother and his cohorts would use, in fact.

And I emphatically Hate Big Brother.

Hope to meet you all soon in public and maybe together we can work this thing out.

----ZER.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: jennifer on June 01, 2006, 04:33:29 PM
An 'OFFICIAL' Hello to Urrisgirl and I guess to Goldfishboy as well. 

This is an awesome thread.  Until Meg started it we were all posting relatively anonymously.  Of course there were the people who knew each other from Freeze Peach - but for those of us not in that neighborhood, it felt anonymous. 

I know a lot of people LIKE the fact that no one knows who they are on the board and that way you can state your mind - however by opening up a little bit we're better able to read our audience.  With some background of one another we have a better chance at clear communication.  We're more likely to "get" the jokes, sarcasm, local language, etc...

In fact I"m sure that the people on the board who have met one another tend to misunderstand each other posts much less frequently than those who have never met the poster.  So i'm advocating - not only for everyone to introduce themselves.... but lets get together and have a group hug  :-D

Aww .... <sniff> You guys are gonna break this cynical girl's heart ... (so be it, means there's still a little left ...). Okay, so here is my official "hello":

Gave away my real name somewhere on the board early on, since then, prefer to be called by my TRX-christened name, "dc" though the alternate "Kerouac Kitty" still makes me laugh ... (google duluoz).

I am a NYC provincial: born and raised in Queens; grew up in Corona, moved to Rockaway, then Forest Hills. Educated fully in the NYC Public schools and attended a CUNY college. Moved to Astoria in February, and it is a rare understatement from me to say that it was one of the best decisions of my life.

As I have said to some of you, I don't know what I would have done had I not found this board. I arrived here a few months after ending a 12-year marriage and after lurking for just a brief while (the posts I place here are my first on any board, too), I was completely taken with the community here; how everyone wrote and interacted; the variety of interests, backgrounds, and personalities; and the topics serious and silly.

Those of you who have met me know I'm pretty much a stubborn, opinionated, melodramatic, wise-a*s, chain-smoking, atheist, only-child, with a fondness for black t-shirts and jeans, mopey song lyrics, books, Smithwick's beer, my zen cat (& original avatar ...) Siddha, her snaggle-toothed brother, Taylor, and hot chocolate with caramel (in lieu of a pot of black coffee).

My personal line of "misanthrope" is (for the most part) said with a wink, but it took every ounce of strength to go out and meet the board members that first night (braving Uncle T's warnings, and all ... heh). And that was perhaps my second best decision. In just four short (long) months, this board has introduced me to some of the most generous, intelligent, fun (and funny), talented, and just plain nice people I've ever come across. It has also brought me to a few people who I hold very, very close to my heart and who I now can't remember having ever lived without (and oh, yeah, I'm a sentimental fool).

And finally, to answer a question I get asked a lot: yes, the avatar drawing really is me, as interpreted by Kyle Baker in his mid-90s New York Magazine comic strip "Late Hit."

So, hello, and a much-belated thank you for my wonderful welcome, and a continuing welcome to those of you who have joined us since.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: nycatexas on June 06, 2006, 01:47:18 AM
Hi Y'all, I only found this board a few months ago but liked it right from the beginning.

On July 4 it will be a year since my husband Max (54) and I (43) moved here from Amarillo, Texas. Despite some health problems we both have faced, the last year has been the happiest of our lives. I've wanted to live in NYC since I was 9 years old. I joined the U. S. Coast Guard after high school in order to have a chance to live here and lived on Governor's Island for 4 incredible years. (If you haven't been on the free tour you HAVE to go - it's awesome.) Also lived in Italy, Connecticut, California and Boston thanks to Uncle Sam.

Had to leave the military to care for my terminally ill father, then my terminally ill mother, then raised my 1-year-old niece because my sister is a low-life criminal and a permanent guest of the Texas Dept. of Corrections. Though I do consider my niece my daughter, I don't have other children (thank God, because one is enough for anybody!) We moved here after she graduated high school. She actually was accepted to a prestigous NYC acting school but after the first semester decided it wasn't for her and she's back in Texas going to college.

I got really sick and almost died from having Diabetes and not knowing it. I spent the entire month of January in Wyckoff hospital in Brooklyn and now am in the best health of my life. My husband had to have heart surgery in April and now he is in the best health of HIS life. So... we are both really happy and really healthy!  :-D He is a RN at Hospital for Special Surgery and I am an unemployed newspaper reporter and freelance writer.  My husband and I also published a history magazine about the Texas Panhandle for a couple of years named "Yesterday's Panhandle". That was a lot of fun!

I love everything about New York City - the history, the architecture, the noise, the tourists, the subway, the quirky stores, I just love it....everyday I walk out the door and think about how happy I am living here! On "our" trains I always sit so I can see the Manhattan skyline coming and going from Astoria. I relish the moments when people ask me for directions because I love knowing NYC. I love telling tourists little known info that makes their trip here better - like they don't have to pay $15 to get into the Met... they can pay as little as a penny. (Get "The Cheap Bastard's Guide to New York City" for more great tips like this!) My husband gets so embarrassed when I do that so he makes me buy the tickets, but I have no qualms about embracing my inner cheap bastard! I'm devouted to my NFT book and don't go anywhere without it.  I still have my Texas accent but often it is hard for people to understand me so I find my enunciation is getting better or, as my friends in Texas say, I sound more like a Yankee everyday.

Other interests are history, reading, trivia, playing yahtzee and card games, beach, people-watching, football (Go Cowboys!), music (both kinds - Country AND Western). Just kidding, that's just one of my little country jokes. Dig the blues (Hound Dog Taylor esp) and also a big Ani DiFranco fan. (So bummed I'll be out of town when she plays SummerStage). Some folks, esp. at first, probably think I am nosey because I ask a lot of questions but that's cause I love meeting people and finding out things about them... their stories, why they do what they do, their experiences...hence the reporter thing.  I love to laugh, sing at the top of my lungs (though my voice could peel paint off the wall) and generally have a good time. Also not afraid to voice my strong opinions.

I also like to talk.....a lot......

I have a couple of NYC friends from the job I had before I got sick but really am desperate to meet new friends, which is one reason I like this board so much. I was really happy to meet some of you at the clothing swap and look forward to meeting everyone! I plan on joining some of your get togethers and hope a Beer Garden outing happens soon. 

Whew.... :-)


Cathy

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: firelight79 on June 14, 2006, 05:00:35 PM
After reading this thread (which has taken me quite some time!) i realized i never said "hello!"
so....
HELLO ASTORIA
  (Hello Jenn)

I'm Jenn, 26 and on my second place in Astoria. I used to live on 30th Ave and 45th street, right near the playground. If i pay real close attention i can spot my old building in certain scenes when i watch a bronx tale. for those that saw the movie, its the corner where the guys randomly beat down the black kids on their bikes.
when my ex and i split i had to give up the apartment (2 BR, the BRs were walk thru though, so a little hard to rent to a stranger. and the landlord lived there and was a little dificult).
so good ole craigslist helped me find my new place on  37th street btwn 34th and 35th ave. (and i traded difficult lives in the bldg landlord for difficulut absentee landlord). i have 2 roommates, one which has been constant since i moved in and the other moved in in january.
I've lived in astoria for 5 years now, right after i graduated with my useless BA in English from Fordham(and my 5 year reunion party-AKA free booze and food night is Friday). This current apartment has been home for 3 years and will be for at least one more.
I currently slave away as an admin/office manager for a neckwear and hosiery firm. i sum up my job as being a monkey puppet. the non fashionista working in fashion, sigh.
my bright spot has been hoping and trying to get into Hunter's graduate program to become a High School English teacher, but alas i have gotten the same "we regret to inform you.." letter 2 years in a row.
formerly grew up in Jackson Hts so i am a total queens girl. if i had any art skills what so ever i would design queens t-shirts and gear a la Brooklyn. but secretly i don't want to advertise astoria for fear i will priced out quicker. i went to HS in the neighborhood. you Fatty's fans dine in what used to be a creepy establishment i used to pass for 4 years while hiking up or down the hill to SJP...the Prep.
i find it amazing how much the neighborhood has changed since i was a teenager. and yet how some of it has stayed the same. ahhh, nostalgia-the Q19A bus ride...
anyhoo I love the recent "explosion" in fun cool things to do and places to go. and yet i feel like i haven't taken full advantage of it. which is sad since i chronicle upcoming astoria events on my website. and i read about all the nifty things going on here that i never seem to make it out to.
in other news about me...i'm about to be divorced...don't worry, i'm happy about that. it was stupid mistake/favor that will thankfully conclude soon. in good relationship news, my BF and i will be celebrating a year together tomorrow  :-D
i found him how i found my apartment, good ole list of craig (ladies do not fear the personal ad!) i forget who asked, and what thread it was on, but someone asked where to find a tool toting irish man, well mine was found on CL. other suggestions would be sunnyside where he lives. the irish woodside boys seem a little more crazy. but quite a delicious accent, yummmmmmmmm.
speaking of delicious, i LOOOOOOOOOVE food. i joke that i cheat on john with food. i'm kinda picky though and i joke that i am the whitest latina (well half, other half being irish) you will meet due to my not being able to tolerate spicy. i'd say its the irish but john eats the thai & indian food (yuck squared!) as well as the spicy mcspicy foods. i'm a plain jane. but i looooove cooking and baking. i make a mean apple pie. i also love throwing parties and entertaining. my friends swear they come to parties for the food i make. i'd love to invite you all to my summer fiesta but there wouldn't be enough room! i like trying new places to eat, but i get trapped into going to the same places b/c i like them. some placies i dig: cafe bar, cup(especially since they changed the menu), cavo, mundo, napoli(shhh keep the best cheap italian food a secret though!), michael's, sunrise(good cheap sushi, especially my fave, the boston roll)...having a brain fart....and over in sunnyside i dig Bliss and Sidetracks.
quick hits of other groovy things...star trek(TNG and Enterprise), stargate, battlestar galactica(noticing a theme?), rescue me, nip/tuck, king of queens(of course!), the office-old and new, dog the bounty hunter-totally wierd guily pleasure, but i kind of watch from an anthropological/sociological standpoint, deadwood....i watch waaaaaaaaaaaay too much TV. oh, John and i were recently on last comic standing! we're superstars!
waiting for superman to finally open. was very disappointed with X3.
love to read, but haven't pick up anything in a bit. i need to go on a good used book hunting trip. not the strand, but a good book stand. i miss the crazy old lady who sold used books on ditmars near the train. i got a lot of good stuff there.
obsessed with music, my mp3's are nearing the 8000 mark and i am always on the lookout for new additions. i'm a total rock n roll, punk, indie sorta gal.
when in the mood i write. haven't really done much of that lately. work has sucked the creative juices out of me.
oh, i'm also longwinded.
so i will shut the heck up now.
feel free to pick my brain should you choose....just leave me something behind...

Jenn

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: mcdirk on June 18, 2006, 11:06:00 PM
I've been posting quite a bit recently, but never formally introduced myself, so here goes.
I've been living in Astoria for 12 years, all in the same apartment on 34th Street, just South of Broadway.  I love the neighborhood - I think Queens is much more diverse and interesting than any other borough). 
I'm very involved in gay politics in NYC - currently I serve as the President of the citywide LGBT political club, Stonewall Democrats of NYC (sdnyc.org) and am active with the Lesbian and Gay Democratic Club of Queens, and more recently the Powhatan Regular Democratic Club here in Astoria (over off Newtown Road).  I like to get involved and joined a local church in the last year, Trinity Lutheran, up on 31st Avenue at 37th Street, as well as got active with the Astoria Kiwanis (though my work).  Professionally, I am the Director of External Affairs for QSAC (Quality Services for the Autism Community), which means I keep elected officials briefed on my organizations goals and needs and try and get them to do more for people with autism, as well as running autism awareness events, writing newsletters and press releases and working with disability groups and councils.  I spend a lot of time in meetings and like to network. 
I tend to get active on animal issues, environmental issues and civil rights issues.  Working with homeless youth and combatting bullying/teaching tolerance in our schools are my main two projects these days.
I love to cook, I love to hear about interesting restaurants and usually check them out (though not if they're seafood places!  ick!)  I am a big indie music fan and get to two or more concerts most months.  Recently I've been getting into Death Cab for Cutie, Tegan and Sara and Rilo Kiley, and I like my old 80s standards.  I have two cats who are the best two cats I know, though they have health issues - one is asthmatic and one is diabetic.  I got one when I was working at the ASPCA, the other found me through friends. 
That's pretty much it!  Feel free to ask questions.

(How many vetoes came from W. Bush?)


http://www.school-house-rock.com/Bill.html

Boy: Whew! You sure gotta climb
a lot of steps to get to this
Capitol Building here in
Washington. But I wonder who
that sad little scrap of paper is?


I'm just a bill.
Yes, I'm only a bill.
And I'm sitting here on Capitol Hill.
Well, it's a long, long journey
To the capital city.
It's a long, long wait
While I'm sitting in committee,
But I know I'll be a law some day
At least I hope and pray that I will
But today I am still just a bill.


Boy: Gee, Bill, you certainly have a lot of patience and courage.
Bill: Well, I got this far. When I started I wasn't even a bill, I was just an idea.
Some folks back home decided they wanted a law passed, so they called
their local Congressman, and said, "You're right, there oughta be a law."
Then he sat down and wrote me out and introduced me to Congress. And I
became a bill, and I'll remain a bill until they decide to make me a law.


I'm just a bill
Yes I'm only a bill,
And I got as far as Capitol Hill.
Well, now I'm stuck in committee
And I'll sit here and wait
While a few key Congressmen discuss
and debate
Whether they should let me be a law.
How I hope and pray that they will,
But today I am still just a bill.


Boy: Listen to those Congressmen arguing! Is all that discussion and debate about you?
Bill: Yeah, I'm one of the lucky ones. Most bills never even get this far. I hope they
decide
to report on me favorably, otherwise I may die.
Boy: Die?
Bill: Yeah, die in committee. Ooh, but it looks like I'm gonna live!
Now I go to the House of Representatives, and they vote on me.
Boy: If they vote yes, what happens?
Bill: Then I go to the Senate and the whole thing starts all over again.
Boy: Oh no!
Bill: Oh yes!


I'm just a bill
Yes, I'm only a bill
And if they vote for me on Capitol Hill
Well, then I'm off to the White House
Where I'll wait in a line
With a lot of other bills
For the president to sign
And if he signs me, then I'll be a law.
How I hope and pray that he will,
But today I am still just a bill.


Boy: You mean even if the Whole Congress says you
should be a law, the president can still say no?
Bill: Yes, that's called a veto. If the president vetoes
me, I have to go back to Congress and they vote
on me again, and by that time you're so old...
Boy: By that time it's very unlikely that you'll become
a law. It's not easy to become a law, is it?
Bill: No!


But how I hope and pray that I will,
But today I am still just a bill.


Congressman: He signed you, Bill!
Now you're a law!
Bill: Oh yes!!!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: abichuela on June 23, 2006, 06:47:49 PM
Hi everyone, I'm Abby. I have lived in Astoria for 5.5 years now, but have only recently realized what a great community is growing here, and am very excited to be more a part of it!  I discovered the board a few months ago, but didn't post til recently (to tell a not-so-pleasant story here: http://astorians.com/index.php?topic=2143.0 ).

I love Astoria and am so happy I ended up here randomly when I moved to New York.  My apartment overlooks the Beer Garden, so it's getting a little loud these days - especially when the Czech Republic gets a goal in the World Cup!  And I love the Beer Garden, but the lines have been getting riDICulous in the past year or so.

What else do I love...  I love cheese!  And exploring new foods and restaurants, summer picnics and winter sledding in Astoria Park, snowboarding, samba, salsa, world music, travel, languages, dolphins, kitties, playing guitar, songwriting, singing, dancing, making lists.  Also my boyfriend Tom (who I invite to introduce himself here!), who stays with me here most of the time and cooks me burgers and Filipino food, and has made an impromptu garden on the fire escape.

What I do...  I currently work as a financial literacy trainer & counselor at a community development credit union in Washington Heights, but am looking for a full-time job in the field of international development/microfinance. 

What have I done...  Studied music and anthropology (ethnomusicology) in undergrad, then lived in Ecuador for a couple years after college, then moved to Astoria and worked at World Music Institute for a couple years, then got my degree at the New School in International Affairs/Socio-Economic Development last year, and here I am ... still in Astoria.

I really hope to meet all of you soon around Astoria, as it seems like such a wonderful, welcoming community!  Though I'm relatively new to this board, I extend my warm welcome as well to those who are newcomers to Astoria!

-Abby

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Namor_X on July 06, 2006, 09:20:48 PM
Hello fellow Astorians.  I've lived on and off in Astoria for years.  I came from East Harlem back in the 70's where my mother moved us to 41st and Bway.  Anyone remember the EE train?  That's our current R train.  It would only go to Lexington and 59th up until 7:30.  You would have to walk to the elevated stop on Bway and 31st st if you wanted to get into Manhattan.  I don't want to explain how you'd get there otherwise.  It was just too long of a trip!

At any rate, after that I've lived all over the place but I'd find myself back in Astoria.  I had gotten married and lived in Alexandria, VA, but when I came back to NY, you guessed it, Astoria.  Then I lived in Manhattan for a while (yeah, the ex-wife has the condo, oh well), and after that I lived in NJ.  But when it came to getting another apartment in NY?  Astoria!  So I've been back since '99 and unless I can get back into Manhattan, this is the place to be!

Hey everbody! Some of you may remember my post (http://www.astorians.com/index.php?topic=2527.0) about apartment hunting a while back. I found a place with ease and I will be moving in a couple weeks from now. Luckily, I found a place one day before the blackout!

Let's see, to formally introduce myself...

I am from Athens, Georgia and have lived here most of my life. (I must say it's a bit comforting moving from one city with a statue of Athena to another.) I am a recent graduate of the University of Georgia. I majored in communications and film studies.

I am a documentary filmmaker, currently in post production with my first feature length documentary. To pay the bills, I spent the summer teaching video production at an academic summer camp.

While in NYC, I plan to pursue my future documentaries, find work with other documentary filmmakers, and will begin my master's degree in media studies in September. So, chalk up another nerd for the academic thread!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Janice on December 07, 2006, 03:32:37 PM
Okay here goes again!  I was born in Flushing Hospital in August of 1943.  I lived the first seven years of my life in Astoria, 33-10 33rd Street.  It was a three story walk up.  Does anyone remember this apartment house?

I remember so many things about living in Astoria during this time.  Christopher Walken's father had the local bakery.  Walken and I are the same age, I think we went to the same PS.

I also remember the monkey grinder, plying his tunes under our apartment window, with his monkey.

I remember black out curtains in our apartment before the war was over.  I rememer hot summers when we slept on the fire escape and when the police opened the fire hydrants in the streets where we would play in the water.  And then come home when we were covered with filth.

I remember my mother told me about "graft" -- I said , what was that?  She told me about the "bad guys" who would throw bricks through the windows of the store fronts if they weren't paid.

I remember the pink balls that were sold at the local drug store that we would bounce on the apartment building walls.  I remember egg creams, that cost a dime.  Egg creams, no eggs, but chocolate syrup and milk and seltzer!  How yummy!

So, we moved out to Long Island in 1950.  To West Hempstead.  To have a better life?  I don't know.  My fondest memories are not from Long Island, but from Astoria.

I haven't been in Astoria for over 50 year.  But it still has my heart.

Any response to this!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: JSmi1978 on January 07, 2007, 11:20:46 PM
Hello All -

I joined Astorians last week. I've actually been posting on some topics but I should have introduced myself first. Sorry about that! Certain posts had me going so I had immediately responded to those.   Im a 28 yr old female working in the Finance industry who has lived in Astoria since 2003.

I came to Astoria by chance. I was living in the Bronx in a really miserable little apartment, when a friend of mine told me she was moving back to Astoria, and asked me if I wanted to be her roommate. I immediately broke my lease and took whatever little money I had and moved in with her. We found an apartment within 3 weeks. It was on 38th street near Steinway. Ok apartment, it was somewhat brand new but my landlord was a bit shady (but nice). It was a 3 bedroom. Actually 2.5 bedroom bc the 3rd bedroom was tiny. We wound up finding a third person on craigslist.com to move in there so our rent was cheaper.

Anyways we stayed there for 1.5 years and then we all decided to go our separate ways because moving in with boyfriends and such.  So I wound up by chance (and I do mean by chance) getting a 1 bedroom apartment over on Crescent Street. Im like 4 long blocks from the subway, but hey I can't complain. I have a friend living in Manhattan whose apartment is the size of my bedroom, so things could have been worse.

So although Ive been here for almost 4 years, im still learning the area. I made that a new years resolution because im always hanging in Manhattan and not taking advantage of whats around the corner from me. Im a big foodie so already this week ive tried many different restaurants and exploring the many different streets in Astoria.

Im a Bronx girl at heart, but Astoria has definately become my adopted hometown!  :-)

Life Drawing was and still is my passion.  As far as how I got into retouching, it was mostly chance.
I had taken a few Photoshop classes through the years and my mom was a photographer, so we messed around with it artistically for years.  Then, about three years ago I got a job in the digital retouching department at Lifetouch NSS.  I turned out to be pretty good at it and ended up running the department before I left to move up here.

I think your right about the drawing, I found that the best retouchers start out as artist.  We just have the eye for detail that comes from years and years of looking for what's wrong with the picture instead of what's right...then working it until it's right (but not overworked, hahahaha ... oh man.)
Either way I like what I do, which is more then a lot of people can say.  I'd like to do high-end retouching, so the ACE and a better portfolio are in the cards for me this year.
And coffee and/or tea sound like a plan, I'll be there in march.
PS. Do you have an on-line portfolio?

My mom always told me there's your vocation to bring sustenance to your life, and your advocation to bring sanity. Unfortunately, I'm not so simple, and lately I've been frustrated with how much I'm not focusing on what I truly love to do.

So I've played around, at the open mic at Waltz, and at Freeze Peach just this last Saturday. Astoria seems like a very creatively inclined community, and I feel that much more close to my goal (being able to sustain myself on my music alone) by just being here.

So with that long-winded introduction, I say hello.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Shifty on January 20, 2007, 11:03:11 PM
Quote from: Janice on December 07, 2006, 03:32:37 PM
Okay here goes again!  I was born in Flushing Hospital in August of 1943.  I lived the first seven years of my life in Astoria, 33-10 33rd Street.  It was a three story walk up.  Does anyone remember this apartment house?

I remember so many things about living in Astoria during this time.  Christopher Walken's father had the local bakery.  Walken and I are the same age, I think we went to the same PS.

I also remember the monkey grinder, plying his tunes under our apartment window, with his monkey.

I remember black out curtains in our apartment before the war was over.  I rememer hot summers when we slept on the fire escape and when the police opened the fire hydrants in the streets where we would play in the water.  And then come home when we were covered with filth.

I remember my mother told me about "graft" -- I said , what was that?  She told me about the "bad guys" who would throw bricks through the windows of the store fronts if they weren't paid.

I remember the pink balls that were sold at the local drug store that we would bounce on the apartment building walls.  I remember egg creams, that cost a dime.  Egg creams, no eggs, but chocolate syrup and milk and seltzer!  How yummy!

So, we moved out to Long Island in 1950.  To West Hempstead.  To have a better life?  I don't know.  My fondest memories are not from Long Island, but from Astoria.

I haven't been in Astoria for over 50 year.  But it still has my heart.

Any response to this!

Wow! Organ grinders, monkeys on 33rd Ave. and blackout curtains in the windows. So, you remember egg creams for 10 cents - - how about a "2 cents plain"?? (Like I would know - - I read about it once; it's a seltzer, with maybe a lemon.) I useta buy em for $1.00 - lemon mandatory - when I worked in interior construction one summer in Midtown. Hah! 50x inflation!!

Anyway Janice, it's as though you lived in the "black-and-white" days - - before Ektachrome. Well, I've been in Astoria 9 years and pretty much loving every minute! It is absolutely great to hear about the "bygone" stuff - - on Thanksgiving I was cooking up a huge feast and expecting my cousins, heard some racket and looking out the kitchen window over the fire escape saw a nicely dressed knot of "middle-aged" folks - - "That used to be a candy store," said one of the ladies," referring to the street level storefronts below my apartment, which are now just somebody's tomb-quiet backoffice. But of course it's fun to think of the kids all running in and out forever, especially in the summer, dashing in from across Astoria Park. Yep, I live on "the Dit."

Cheers to you in Hempstead or the Hamptons, or Hyannis, or wherever - - from the Hellgate, dahlink!

Post by: Hardkore on February 01, 2007, 02:56:11 PM
Quote from: token4 on February 01, 2007, 01:45:26 PM
Hey all!  This is Thomas the new kid on the block.  Just moved into Astoria - Crescent between 23rd and 24th Avenue - with my two roommates this January.  I moved here from Washington Heights, Manhattan.

So here's a question - what is your favorite restaurant in the Ditmars Blvd area?

Best,
Thomas

I can tell you I do NOT recormmend El Olivo- People may disagree with me but while the sangria was great, the paella was tasteless and the shellfish hadn't been properly cleaned, and shrimp had been overcooked. I left feeling heavy and bogged down with gross food.

I also do not recommend Kyklades, which I'm sure has a following but I didn't get a fresh fish sense from the place, it tasted the same as microwave dinners.

I love Watanabe, Wave Thai, Ubols, and the Igloo cafe does a decent burger.

Trundle and Capibara, I have spent a little time in Mpls and really enjoyed my time there.  When I visit, I stay with friends in Nordeast, which is a nice neighborhood - their house is beautiful!  They bought it for a song in the early-90s, those lucky ducks.  When I would visit, we would either all go out to Club Velvet to see King Kini spin, or First Ave and dance the night away (my friend ran the VIP room there).  We'd have a late breakfast the next morning at the Egg & I.  Have also enjoyed The Modern, too.  I had a few friends who ran Bitstream Underground, which also had a BBS, which was a fun virtual place to hang out.  I'm still in touch regularly with people I met on that BBS.

Loved walking around the Lake of the Isles, too.

I seriously considered moving to Mpls, as I think it's a wonderful regional center, but it's just too cold for me.

Thought I'd throw my hat into the ring and say hi as well.  I'm Michael, and I'm new to these boards but certainly not to Astoria...I was born in Astoria just over 22 years ago at the now defunct Boulevard Hospital (anyone remember it???) and have spent most of my life in Astoria, complete with a Greek upbringing!  I've moved around a lot within Astoria too...first lived near 34th Avenue and Steinway, later a bit closer to Broadway, then on 46th Street a few steps from the station and the everpresent corner donut shop, before moving north to Steinway and 21st, then to 28th Street south of Broadway, then back up to Ditmars and Crescent.  I made the rounds in school as well...St. Catherine's, PS 166, PS 70, PS 84, PS 122 before going to High school in the city and being one of only two Astorians in my grade!  My living situation has now taken me to Flushing, but it's still close enough that I manage to make it into Astoria several nights per week.

I've had fun browsing the boards thus far and look forward to being a part of the discussions.  I was also pleasantly surprised to see three Stony Brook alums just from the first page of this thread alone! I'm a Political Science major from Stony Brook University, where I also am about to receive my Masters.

Hi everyone! This is my first time posting on Astorians.com, which I've been reading for a few months now. I moved to Astoria with my boyfriend in October 2006 and love it! I went to Boston University and currently am getting my Masters in Library & Information Science at Long Island University at their Manhattan satellite campus (nyu's bobst). I work full-time for a major publishing company, where the only perk is all the free books I could ever imagine.

I love Astoria so far... my family has a long history with Astoria. My grandfather grew up in Astoria and loves to tell stories about watching the Triboro Bridge being built. My father spent the first few years of his life in Astoria as well.

My one and only complaint about Astoria so far? The few blocks around my Ditmars-area apartment are always covered in dog poop! Other than the constant fear of stepping in it (again), me and my boyfriend are very happy here!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Harlan on March 18, 2007, 11:30:02 AM
Welcome from another Shampoo-Banana refugee! Who will you be translating for? A friend of mine is an interpreter for the UN...

There are lots and lots of other foodies on this board...

As for movies, you'll find that it's very easy to get down to the Village where most of the foreign/indie films are. There are half a dozen theaters that show nothing but. (This said, cool as the Tribeca film festival is, I do miss Ebertfest...)

It's possible to bike to Manhattan, certainly, but it's not exactly pleasant. Traffic is extremely heavy, and NYC has not yet figured out how to make bike commuting very easy, especially from Queens. (There are some wonderful bike paths along the Hudson.) Do a google search for "transportation alternatives", though, and you can find some activism in that area.

I think you'll be very impressed by the green grocers in Astoria. Wide variety, usually very good quality, and pretty inexpensive. For organic/natural foods, the Union Square greenmarket (40 minutes away on the N train) is 4 days a week, and is one of the better greenmarkets in the country. And you should definitely consider one of the two Astoria CSAs...

Hope your move goes well!

Interesting about the thin walls. I'm not sure if you'd need board approval, but if you want to spend a little money, you could probably hang soundproofing drywall over your existing walls and significantly improve the quietness of your new apartment before you turn around and sell it! (Google "soundproof drywall" for more information.) I know even just a 2nd layer of standard drywall helps some, but the fancier stuff helps a lot more. You can also soundproof windows too, by installing a separate set of panes on the inside of the window, with like a 3" gap. I believe that floors and ceilings are a whole lot trickier...

And welcome, Jay!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Starwind51 on June 07, 2007, 06:55:43 PM
Hello All.  I am Starwind51.  Call me Star.  My name used to be Blue Wind, (no, really, my name used to be Blue Wind), but when I started posting things online and needed an e-mail address, SOMEONE at Yahoo was already using my name!  I had to think up a new name and Starwind seemed a pretty substitute.  Since I was joining an X-Files group, 51 (as in Area 51) was an appropriate number.

I was born in Manhattan.  My family lived in Kips Bay.  I actually used to live at "toidy-toid and toid" (Third Avenue at 33rd Street.)

We moved to Astoria/LIC when I was a baby.  I've lived in A/LIC for 50 of my 51 years.  I inherited my phone number from my mother when she moved away, so I've had the same phone number for 50 years!  In fact, aside from relatively brief periods when I moved away (I moved, not my stuff, which was left at Mom's), I've lived on the same street pretty much all my life.

For most of my life, if you said "I live in Long Island City" to someone not from the area they would think you lived on Long Island or lived in a factory.  So I started saying I live in Astoria.  Actually I live in either the Long Island City end of Astoria or the Astoria end of Long Island City, depending on what map you look at.  I put Astoria as my address.

I am a multi-faceted person, but I think I'll express my facets elsewhere around the forum rather than list my attributes here.  The following smilies are not really a message, I just like the way they look.

 :evil: :lmao: :angel: :2cool: :smitten:

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Starwind51 on June 10, 2007, 02:39:42 AM
Quote from: erinsdad on June 08, 2007, 05:07:56 PM
Just another new resident. Have lived in Manhattan all my life, and needed a change. Looking for fun bars, interesting people, and whatever else. I'm a single dad, with a ten year old daughter who will be visits every two weeks, and already loves the area. If any one has ideas about kid friendly stuff, I would greatly appreciate it. Otherwise, it's great to find a site like this. 

My nephews love the playground at PS 112 (Crescent St btwn 36 & 37 Aves).  Later in the summer there will be children's concerts.  I guess you could check the Parks Department website to find the list.

Queens has a separate library system from the NYPL, so check the QPL (as well as the NYPL) website for kids events at the different branches.  Visiting different library branches is a great way to get to know different neighborhoods.

Quote from: Astoria Luv on June 11, 2007, 10:33:14 AM
Welcome Chris.  I'm surprised no one had that moniker/name!

I remember when the Astoria realtors had the phrase "best kept secret" in their ads.  As a matter of fact, I think Aamen realty, which used to be inside of the Ditmars train station used the phrase in their ads.


No question about it.   I don't think I'd ever been to Astoria before I moved here.   The reason I knew about it was because a roommate I had in Manhattan was looking to move out and mentioned he was considering Astoria.     When I lost the lease on my Manhattan apartment my plan was to check out neighborhoods in the boroughs and select the one I liked best.   Because my roomie had mentioned Astoria, I started here first, liked what I saw, and got an apartment the same day.   

In fact, I remember that day when I came out here I had an old subway map that showed the R going to Astoria where the N now goes and the N going to where the R goes (at least I think that is what happened).   In any event, I ended up on Northern Boulevard and 48th Street and remember walking down Northern Boulevard and then walking down 31st Street to Broadway where I found some realtors.   I paid $600 in '87 for a two-bedroom apartment on the second floor of a private house on 32nd Street between Broadway and 34th Street.    I moved to another -- rent stablized -- apartment in '01 when the owner wanted to raise my rent from like $1,000 to $1,800.   I said "bye, bye."  Astoria was no longer a secret.   '01 was, if you recall, when the "Times" ran a piece about our little secret and interest in the neighborhood soared.
Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Starwind51 on June 11, 2007, 06:41:11 PM
As a loooooong time resident of Astoria, I of course welcome all of you, but I always hope nobody else finds out about our little neighborhood.  Ahh, stories us old-timers could tell you, of when a house was a house, the sidewalks were slate, the roads were cobblestone, and the horse drawn wagon was a mystery.

The horse drawn wagon still is a mystery, because nobody ever thought to call out to the driver "hey, where do you keep the horse at night???", though after all these years, it has occured to me that he would have just called back "IN A STABLE!!!".  (Late 50's - early 60's.)
Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Chris on June 11, 2007, 09:34:50 PM
Quote from: Starwind51 on June 11, 2007, 06:41:11 PM
As a loooooong time resident of Astoria, I of course welcome all of you, but I always hope nobody else finds out about our little neighborhood. 

Unfortunately, I think the cat is out of the bag and has been out since '01 when the "Times" ran a piece on our "little neighborhood."   It cost me dearly, specifically I had to move.   And try getting a seat on the subway in the morning or at midnight.   

Way back in '89, when I was in Astoria for less than two years, I rode to work with a older guy, partially retired, who grew up in Astoria and lived here all his life and the stories he used to tell!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Astoria Luv on June 12, 2007, 08:57:32 PM
Quote from: KatieP311 on June 12, 2007, 10:59:10 AM
Someone please help me with some Astoria insider info!

Thanks  :-D

Welcome KatieP311!  You've come to the right place to learn about the neighborhood.  I've been here for over ten years and I have scratched the surface.  Depending on what your scene and interests are, the area has so much to offer.  I'm sure other folks can give you more specific advice, but I would personally start with a walking tour of the area and explore.  Luckily, you have an advantage since you already the main roads and, having read some of these posts, are familiar with the names of the places that are brought up often, like Freeze Peach.

I usually stay in southern Astoria, but based on what I've read, I find myself going north of 30th Avenue more often.

Before I ask the group about specific places, events or locations, I usually go to the Search bar located at the top of the screen, directly under the banner and enter some key words and up pops threads that discuss, critique and direct me.  However, sometimes new places open and it never hurts to ask  :mrgreen:

Again, welcome to the board and the neighborhood!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: gunsnrosie on June 17, 2007, 03:46:38 PM
Ciao, tutti!

I just joined this community last night and I am very glad I found it! I have lived in Astoria for -2 months: That's right, I said *negative*.  I am planning to move there in August, and am both very excited and quite nervous about the whole thing.  I've never used a broker before and from what I've read on astorians.com and from what my friends who already live there have told me, a broker is the best way to go about finding an apartment there. I also think it'll be the best option for me since almost all of my time is being sucked away by the Intensive ancient Greek program I'm enrolled in for the summer. Intrigued? You should be!  :wink:

My interest in Astoria is multi-fold. In part the move would make my commute to school and work a lot easier that what I have to endure now (I say 'endure' because I live in Briarwood/ Jamaica now and I have to leave about 1.5 hours earlier than any appointments if I want any hope of getting there on time. My school and up-coming-fall-semester job are on the Upper East Side, and I tell ya, sitting on the F train for 45 minutes BEFORE waiting for a bus transfer is NOT good times!). But even more importantly than that, I really love the family/ close-knit neighborhood feel that comes across so clearly on these threads.  Plus: I'm Italian-American (my parents are immigrants so I always seek out chances to speak Italian. Any Italians out there in Astoria?) and my boyfriend is Greek (and I'm making him teach me as much Greek as possible). I figure: with so much Mediterraneaneity apparently running rampant in Astoria: where else could I imagine living?   :mrgreen:

I'm a 28 year old graduate student in archaeology and art history, and I do a lot of photography on the side. Well, when I find some spare moments between writing papers and digging up ancient artifacts. I've read some great things on here about the creative atmosphere in Astoria, and am really looking forward to meeting other artistic types and sharing in the creative vibes.

Reading through these 45 (!) pages of Hello! thread has also fully confirmed for me that Astoria is what I'm looking for. I was lucky enough to have had two great apartments in the last three years with great friends as roommates, but now that it is time for me and my massive library to branch out on our own, I think that we will be quite happy in Astoria.  Ain't that right, libri miei??

Also, though I'm not British, I may have to rival Preston for the title of "Person who says 'Cheers' a lot".  I picked that up a long time ago from a friend who had studied in Edinburgh and it stuck.  Other interesting/weird/ better-you-find-out-now things about me: I'm an unapologetic dork for things Ancient Greek and Roman, hence I like me a good historical fiction novel. I'm an uncloseted Star Wars junkie (I think I will fit in just fine with the massive # of other Sci-Fi freaks here: helloo!); Eddie Izzard cracks me up so hard I actually hurt myself from laughing too hard, and I tend to make up words that do not officially exist (yet) or massacre existing words to the point of utter manglage.  I attribute this both to my belief that there actually aren't enough words in the English language to cover all desired options for expressing oneself, and to the fact that I was/am obsessed with Buffy the Vampire Slayer, a show which made more fully appreciate the sublime beauty of the really bad pun. Oh, and I tend to randomly quote pop culture references I like, which is why I may sometimes be heard talking in French about cheeky monkeys driving buses, but in a British accent.  :evil:

So yes. I figure I ought to end this ridiculously long Hello post, and let you fine people get a word in edgewise.  Here's to being one of you soon! (I hope!)
-Cheers!

Hi Everyone,

I have been reading this site for about a year now and wanted to introduce myself to everyone. I'm a 28 year old writer/student/office drone. I have lived in Queens my whole life and moved to Astoria about two years. I have been told that I look like Quentin Tarantino if his mother was impregnated by a leprechaun. So ummm, I have that going for me. The biggest thing I love about Astoria is that I can have a perfect weekend without leaving my zip code. Bike over the bridge and around Randell's Island. Relax with a book at the park. Lunch at Papa's. Drinks at the garden (or sparrow if the garden is too crowded). Trivia night at the rover. What a town! Thanks for all the help in finding good eats, cold drinks and everything in between.

Cheers and lets go mets!

Kev.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Astoria Luv on July 14, 2007, 11:42:51 AM
Welcome, Sintex.  I feel like one in every five people I meet are originally from Ohio  :-D

You came to the right spot to get connected to the neighborhood!  Whether you want to know which restaurant to go to (or avoid, but you can make your own decision), events in the neighborhood, whether political or social, or just to chat, Astorians is definitely the place to be.

If you get a chance, you should just get out and start walking around.  This area is unique because it's so close to Manhattan, but it has single family homes with quiet, tree lined streets and a nice big ole park on the northwest corner. 

Again, welcome to the area and if you need any help trying to find anything, let us know.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: MFdobbs on July 19, 2007, 09:12:54 PM
Hello all; I'm new.  I actually created my first post in the 'where you're from' thread, but I think it is also pretty applicable here, so I'll just go ahead and add an expanded version to this thread.  SO....

I graduated from school in the summer of '06 (Washington State Univ.), and which point I moved from Seattle to Hoboken with my college girlfriend who had already lined up a cush job for herself.  Essentially, I tagged along in the name of "love."  In record time, however, I managed to break up with the girlfriend, and had to decide whether to stay in NY or go back to Seattle.  By then I had landed a good job in the city, which made the decision a bit more difficult.  Suffice to say, I decided to keep the job and stay, even though I knew relatively no-one in NY beyond my coworkers.  Upon searching Craigslist for a good 2 months, I eventually found a reasonably priced studio in Astoria, NY.  Hadn't heard much about the place, but the rent was right and the commute is a beautiful thing, so to Astoria I came.

In my short stint in Astoria I'd have to say there are definitely more positives than negatives.  Much is undiscovered as of yet.  I'm in the Ditmars area right by the Beer Garden.

Also, my ancestors are Greek, so my last name apparently affords me some instant street-cred around the 'hood.  I know nothing of Greek culture, however, but that's hardly common knowledge.

See ya around the forum, all.

Hello there.

I'm a 34-year-old writer moving down August 1 from Boston, where I've lived since 1991. I'm relocating to NYC mostly because it's there, but also because I figured it'd be a good place to promote my book. I plan to spend time in Manhattan, of course, but it would be really great to find some people with whom to roam Astoria/LIC (I believe there's a place called Fatty's near my house). I've heard mostly great things about Astoria, and when the complaints are along the lines of "we could use a good bookstore" and "sometimes the beer garden gets a little crowded," I know I have little to worry about.

You know, since I have access to all this Astorian brainpower, might I ask a couple of questions?

Is there a way into Brooklyn other than taking the Metro into Manhattan, then out again?

I live near the Ditmars subway stop. Where's a good place to get a drink in that area? I'm a little weary of Irish pubs, but I'm generally happy to try anyplace where I won't get beaten with a pool cue or something.

Hope you're all well.
Jason

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Astoria Luv on July 22, 2007, 11:23:33 AM
Quote from: jasonsr on July 21, 2007, 10:14:28 PM
Is there a way into Brooklyn other than taking the Metro into Manhattan, then out again?


If you're coming from Ditmars, the best way to Pacific Street, which I believe is close to downtown Brooklyn, is actually the N train as it goes directly into Brooklyn after Canal Street, skipping the downtown stops.  If you're going to Williamsburg/Greenpoint and don't mind transfers, you can do the following: Take the N to Queensborough Plaza and catch the 7 going to the city across the platform.  Take this train one stop to 45th Road and follow the signs for the free transfer at 23rd/Ely which is below ground to the G.  I have attached the link to the NYC subway map.

http://www.mta.info/nyct/maps/submap.htm

Quote from: jasonsr on July 21, 2007, 10:14:28 PM
I live near the Ditmars subway stop. Where's a good place to get a drink in that area? I'm a little weary of Irish pubs, but I'm generally happy to try anyplace where I won't get beaten with a pool cue or something.

There are other members who have more knowledge of the drinking establishments in the Ditmars area, but I personally like Stini Yamas on Ditmars between 37th and 36th Street.  They have a nice backyard and the bartenders and staff, at least the ones I met were awesome.  I forgot her name, but one of the bartenders actually remembered what I drank the last time I was there. 

Good luck on your move!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Cotto on August 09, 2007, 06:43:19 PM
Hi everyone. My girlfriend found this board and started posting earlier this summer. I've found myself looking at it frequently, so I figured I might as well sign up too. I was born and raised in Florida but feel at home with the variety and culture of New York. My girlfriend and I have lived here (just off the Astoria Blvd. stop on the N/W line) since September '06. We're both doctoral students who rarely have any free time during the school year but have been fortunate to have the time to explore Astoria this summer. My favorite finds (some thanks to this board):

1. Agnanti (though I swear that dessert tastes like honey nut cheerios in cake form. This is sort of a good thing)
2. Il Bambino (not just the food, but the iced coffee is phenomenal!)
3. Pasta Fina (can be inconsistent, but the personal margherita pie is outstanding)
4. Astoria Park (I love frisbee)
5. Bohemian Hall and Beer Garden (somehow have only been once, but the name says it all)

I want to say thanks to everyone here who ended up helping us have a fantastic summer exploring this great little place!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: vincie on August 21, 2007, 11:36:15 PM
Dear Folks:

Hello.  I've been in Astoria for one year (this time around), and finally got focused enough to register on this board. 

I love it here.  I can't say enough good things about this neighborhood.  The people, the architecture (there are some very lovely houses here, despite all the recent development), the food, the bars, the park.  Not to mention the convenience of living in a nabe full of supermarkets, low-cost stores, and cafes that aren't Starbucks, and being able to commute to Manhattan or Brooklyn in about 30 minutes.

I'm a film person - I write and direct (doesn't earn the bread), and production manage and line produce (does earn the bread).  I didn't realize when I moved here that there were so many artists, musicians, writers, and fellow film-folk already out here.

Okay, that's enough love for now.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: DrewDavidson on September 23, 2007, 12:30:12 PM
Greetings, Astorians!

I've been checking out the board for a while and recently signed up. I'm moving into Astoria next month to expand my meager acting experience (though I'm mid-aged, I've only been acting the past 6 years). I fell in love with the town five years ago when I stayed in Ditmars for two weeks while rehearsing for a tour. I feel very safe here, even at night, and I love the international flavor, the great produce markets on 30th Ave, and the best sidewalk vendors in the five boroughs. This site has been a great education (especially the eye-opening 'bed-bug' thread). Thanks for all the helpful information! See you all around town...

Drew Davidson, actor and newbie poster

Welcome back (soon)!

I live near Ditmars, but have only been there for the last year. Mike's Diner is still there, but on Ditmars and 31st, there's a Starbucks, a bank, a pizza place and a flower shop--no old lady clothes! (Unless it's a door or two back and I haven't noticed it.) Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Astoria Luv on January 02, 2008, 11:30:36 AM
Quote from: nycmizzou on December 30, 2007, 11:18:21 PM
Hi everyone,

I'm Meaghan, and I'm moving to Astoria in just a few days around 36th Avenue.  From what I've seen so far, this website is a great place to pick up the best (and some of the worst) the area has to offer.  I'm very excited to move to Astoria, as I've heard many many positive things. 

I know there are many posts with many good places to go and shop and whatnot but, I was hoping to maybe save myself some time and was wondering if you all could each recommend maybe one restaurant, grocer, gym, bookstore, fun place, etc. that I might want to try in Astoria or in Manhattan.

Thanks All!

Hey Meaghan, here are my own choices, based on seven years on 36th Avenue and eighteen years in the NYC area.

Supermarket: Bravo Supermarket. 34-12 34th Avenue (if you need something quick, go to Food World on 36th Avenue and 31st Street, but make sure you check the expiration dates  :x.  I was burnt too many times).

Restaurant: There are so many choices in the area.  However, since we don't know what your particular taste is, and since you limited it to one, I would recommend The Cup 35-01 36th St.  They have decent food at affordable prices.  They have a good weekend brunch, but expect to wait.

Bookstore: Astoria lacks a chain bookstore, which has been point of contention on the board.  There is a small, family operated (I believe) bookstore on Broadway called Seaburn, 33-18 Broadway, Astoria.  Broadway, in case don't know, is the next stop north on the N/W from 36th Avenue.  There is a Borders on Park Avenue and 57th Street and a Barnes and Noble in Forest Hills on 70th Avenue and Austin Street.

Fun Place: Depends really on what you consider fun.  I've become sort of a regular at a pool/lounge/bar called Clic, at 32-04b Broadway, again one stop away or a quick 8 to 10 minute walk from 36th Avenue and 32nd Street.

Gym: Somebody else is going to have to help you out on that one. 

Hope this helps.  I'm sure people on the board have different ideas and it really depends on what your tastes/interests are.  The great thing about living in NYC, in particular, is that there seems to be something for everyone.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: astoriagirl on January 02, 2008, 09:41:49 PM
Hey Meaghan -

Welcome to Astoria.  The best gym is the NY Sports Club, corner of Steinway St & 30th Ave.  If you want to get a trainer, get Brooke - she's the best.  Kind of pricey, but really knows what she's talking about and teaches a great Pilates class.  For yoga, if you're into that, Paul on Saturday mornings is excellent - but you have to sign up a day in advance.

Like someone else said - restaurants - there are so many it's hard to recommend one.

For cool clothes - try Candy Plum - I forget where it is exactly - but it has a lot of handmade, unusual clothes and jewelry.

I know you already got directed to the Wingtacular at Dillinger's coming up! Also, never be afraid to just say "Hey everybody, come meet me here!" I know that one board member in particular cultivated bunches of friends before she even moved here by making everyone go drink with her when she was up looking at apartments!

Freeze Peach is a great little cafe on 29th Street, almost on the corner of Ditmars. They make a mean latte and have lots of great teas. Internet access is free with purchase of a beverage, so it's a great place to hang if your service is having glitches or you're waiting to get connected. You'll find, also, that most of us on this board are really interested (for the most part) in the more Mom&Pop kind of place than a big chain, so we're always on the hunt for local coffee shops, restaurants and the like!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: caroslime on February 24, 2008, 04:26:00 PM
Hi, y'all!  My husband and I (29 and 30, respectively) moved to the Ditmars/Steinway area in September.  I found Astorians.com during our apt search, and it has been an invaluable resource since.  I've been lurking here for recommendations for everything from apartment brokers to our vet, all with great success.  Thought I'd finally jump into the fray.

I'm originally from the Philly suburbs, moved to NY three years ago (almost to the day!) when my now husband got transfered back to NY for work.  My husband was born in Queens, grew up on LI, so NY really feels like home to him.  We lived in Marble Hill (the Bronx) and Briarwood (way far out in Queens), which were both OK, but now that we found an apartment / neighborhood we both really love in Astoria, it finally feels like home to me too.  I love the quiet, family feel of our street, but it's just a couple blocks away from all the restaurants, bars, and shops on Ditmars.  We both love to cook, and the availability of fresh and unusual ingredients is so incredible that we've forgone exploring the amazing array of restaurants around here.  I figure, we'll leave that until the summer when it's too hot to cook.  Plus, we have plenty of time for all that, because plan to stay here for a long, long time. 

I've been working as an event planner for the last six years, and I love it.  I'm actually looking for a new job, so if you know anyone that could help on that front, I would be eternally grateful...unemployment has me more than a little stir crazy at the moment.  My husband is a 2L at CUNY Law, a total overachiever who works/studies constantly.  So in addition to killing time on the boards here, it would be great to make some new friends in the neighborhood to hang out with while he studies. 

Thanks for such an awesome resource on our awesome community!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: flikchik on February 26, 2008, 09:39:15 PM
Hi to all my fellow Astorians!

I'm a 3rd generation Astoria native.  My Grandparents migrated here from Italy.  After getting married I moved to Bayside, and after getting divorced I wised up and moved back to Astoria.

To all those who are new here....Welcome!  You have made the wise choice to live in a neighborhood that welcomes the new yet continues to keep and cherish it's old world traditions. 

We have the beautiful Astoria Park as our backyard, complete with our ever present towering parents of the neighborhood: the Tri-Borough and Hell Gate Bridges.

And to those who attended PS 122, or took religious classes at Immaculate Conception or who remember what once was "up Ditmars" (aka as 31st Street): The bowling alley (now Keyfood), the movie theater (now a Post Office) Phil's Deli - who had THE best hot dogs and (now a fish store)  I'd love to hear from any of my fellow old time neighbors.  (please tell me 45 is not that old!)  :wink:

Jenny

Hi everyone! i just moved to Astoria about 2 weeks ago and love it so far. My question is this....where would be the best place to start meeting people? I am single and in my early thirties and would like to find a nice, fun place to hang out on the weekends.
Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Rain on March 16, 2008, 05:33:41 PM
Hey Robynlynn,
There are so many places to hang out in Astoria. Numerous cafes along Broadway and 30th Avenue. One of my faves is Cafe Bar on 36th Street and 34th Avenue (most Astorians call it "No Name" because it doesn't have an actual name:)
It has a bohemian and low-key atmosphere.
While I usually go there with friends, I have gone plenty of times just solo and always struck up conversations with interesting and cool people.

Also Hellgate Social is a great bar on 12th Street and Astoria Blvd. It's open and friendly and doesn't usually have cliques hanging about that would make it awkward to go there and meet new people.

Island is a fairly new club/lounge that opened up on 35th Avenue and 36th Street. It is a nice place but the last time I was there (on a Saturday) it was infested with LI guidos. Also, prices are typical of a Manhattan bar.

Here's another hello from another newbie!

My name's Jen, and I've lived in Astoria for 8 years (after 8 in Brooklyn and 6 in Manhattan; before that I lived in Iowa). My husband (who also had been living in & loving Astoria for a while when we met 3 years ago) and I live near the park and enjoy growing things in our little front & back yards (this year we have tomatos, radishes, lettuce, strawberries, blackberries, peppers & lots of flowers -- but the squash borers are eating our zucchinis). We have way too many books & spend a lot of time exploring our city & beyond. We're also expecting our first child in September :-)

It's been great to read through this thread and discover this community. It kind of feels like when I first started paying attention to birds, and learning their calls, and suddenly there was a whole other layer of life I'd never been aware of before (for the record, I've seen over 20 species of birds in Astoria park/surrounding neighborhood so far, which is kind of amazing for such an urban environment I think).

Look forward to reading more and being part of this community.

Jen

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: jenr on July 15, 2008, 07:51:54 PM
thanks for the welcomes!

I do love Astoria Park, elkelorraine. there is always so much to see, whenever you go!

Bentleys Dad, wow, 7 dozen zucchini flowers!!! amazing. did you fry them up? yum. The squash borer is a flying insect that deposits its eggs actually inside the squash plant's stems. so when the larvae hatch, they start chowing down on the insides of the stems, nasty. once they are there there's not much you can do, although we've found sites that recommend trying to kill the larvae by poking pins into the stems or using a razor blade to excise them. The problem is that although you can tell they're in the plant somewhere (flowers don't lead to healthy fruits, stems begin to wilt and blacken for no apparent reason) it's hard to know exactly where -- and if you go poking & slashing everywhere it's not so good for the plant either :-( Apparently you can also try wrapping tin foil around the stems when they're still small, which theoretically prevents the adult from poking her ovipositor through the stem. Maybe we'll try this with a second crop, there should be time if we do it now!
good luck with the tomatoes!

as for the books -- agreed, but we've gotta make some room for the tot :-)
 
Title: Re: Hello

He friend, welcome home. Wife and I live on that same block from your past.  Was Newtown always so dirty?

Take the n or w train to Ditmars and catch the bus to 21st street.  There should also be a bus on 21st street from QP to 24th ave or Ditmars.  That should be the closest stops to the park.  Keep your eye open for the Red tailed hawks living in the park. Quite a sight.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: trolleydude on August 16, 2008, 10:07:12 AM
Quote from: Pulled pork on August 15, 2008, 10:19:16 PM
He friend, welcome home. Wife and I live on that same block from your past.  Was Newtown always so dirty?

Newtown Rd. was always a little seedy as a kid since it was the back side of the apartments and the stores on Steinway St. Consequently, it was a out of sight out of mind most time so trash and graffiti happened. It was also a great place for kids to get away from the eyes of the parents on 41st St. so most stickball and ace,king,queen games happened back there. There was a Kings outlet up Newtown by the gas station and that attracted some foot traffic, but Newtown was a great place to hang out.

Take the n or w train to Ditmars and catch the bus to 21st street.  There should also be a bus on 21st street from QP to 24th ave or Ditmars.  That should be the closest stops to the park.  Keep your eye open for the Red tailed hawks living in the park. Quite a sight.

Last year when we were there we were swarmed by squirrles. The hawks must be fat by now.

If you look around this site you will find tons of suggestions of great places to eat, see, etc...  Enjoy your trip home.

I have and Rizzo's is on the list as usual.

Is there a chance you will be around the week of 9/7-9/13 so we could meet on 41st somewhere. GF would love to see inside one of the buildings. My Dad was the super at 30-41 and I had to clean the banisters and oil them almost every Saturday. The trip down memory lane would be awesome.
