Title: Re: Hello
Post by: paratactical on August 18, 2008, 04:05:30 PM
Hey--

Others might disagree with me, but if she's not street smart and she's going to be on her own frequently, stay near the N.

I'm a lady of diminutive stance and if I had moved to a place where I had to use the Steinway stop and ride the R/E/V to get around, I would not have felt very comfortable. I think that the N/W has problems, but comes more often and since the line ends in Astoria, it doesn't have a bunch of people trying to get further out to nastier 'hoods at night. I feel 1,000 times safer on the N/W than I do on the R. It's probably not true and probably just a feeling, but if your lady isn't street savvy and will be on her own, she'll probably be a lot more comfortable closer to the N/W.
Title: Re: Hello
Post by: daisy on August 18, 2008, 07:49:32 PM
Quote from: alv on August 18, 2008, 03:53:01 PM
Do homework? Classes? :)
Its been a long time since I have had homework. 5th year here :) Unfortunately, I get to teach, and that means explaining to other people how to do homework.
Oh, and my commute is worse. I go to school in New Haven, CT.  :| My commute is going to be 3 hours each way. However, I will probably just do it twice a week and spend the night at a friend's place, or just sleep in my office.

My fiancee, she will have to commute every day. Speaking of commutes, I have had a horrendous experience trying to get from Steinway to midtown this Saturday. No train for like 20 minutes during the day. Is that typical of that line? Should I try to stay closer to the N?

Also, are there any areas where a girl should not walk alone from the subway at around midnight. I am not really worried about myself, but I would not describe my fiancee as street smart.
While I can't speak for other people's experiences, I've lived on both the R and the N/W lines in Astoria for many years.  Neither line has been more uncomfortable than the other for me.  You get the same amount of drunks and homeless after midnight on the trains, and the walks home have been quiet but not any more dangerous than anywhere else.  Astoria is a mostly safe area, but you should always be aware of your surroundings as you would anywhere alone at night.  Crime happens here, and near either line.  But I wouldn't categorize Astoria as dangerous at all.  I'd be more concerned about how long your walk is to the train, than which line it is on.  As far as wait time goes, unfortunately, 20 mins wait time on the weekends and late nights is common on both lines, and is common for a lot of the NYC trains, not just ours.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: evxplant on February 10, 2009, 02:31:46 AM
I've been hearing a lot about burglaries, some robberies, and that rapist running around, and as a native NYer I can tell you it's nothing shocking considering the current economic times.  Conventional wisdom applies: try not to walk in desolate areas by yourself at night (girls AND guys!), get yourself some mace, take a self defense class, take a cab home, or get a big dog if your landlord allows it. Avoid living near "borderline" areas, aka, within spitting distance of the projects...because it doesn't take nearly as much effort to walk over 2 blocks to snatch your purse as it does to try to get a damn job. 

Have your keys in your hand--in fact, palm them and make a fist around them, with a key sticking out  between each finger.  Have your phone handy. Let your friends know when you've arrived home. Let someone know you're COMING home! Don't listen to your ipod when you're walking down the street in the middle of the night.  Travel in packs.  Look behind you.  Know where there is a business that is open late or 24 hrs in the vicinity where you're walking so that you can find someone to help you if you catch some creep following you.

I am a native Manhattanite cheating on the LES with Astoria.  We absolutely love our new home, and plan on raising our kids here.  I'm a bartender/cosmetology student by day and my fianc is a graphic designer.  One of the best things about Astoria is all the great shops (especially the bakeries, YUM, MARTHA'S!) and the fact that small business can thrive here. There is a lot of stuff to do without having to go trekking into the LES or East Village like all the wannabes, college kids, and all of New Jersey, and it's more affordable and chill.  The charm of the area is that homey sense of old school community, like I remember the NYC of my childhood being before the Starbucks-ification began...just, you know, with fewer crack dealers. A LOT FEWER. 

This neighborhood is pretty tight knit and safe, but just remember that you're still in a large City and the rules of common sense apply.  You've made a good choice moving here!  Enjoy the area, Hope, and welcome!

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: Insanefane on June 24, 2009, 10:43:58 PM
Hello All

     I just want to introduce myself. Most people in the neighborhood know me as Fane! Those that do are more than likely in thier 40's or 50's. Anyone who has hung out in astoria park in the last decade would recognize us. Us being me and the couple of old friends that i still get together with. We usually hang out in the area that we refer to as the triangle. This is becuase the foot paths roughly form a triangle. Its above the meadows towards 19th street near the hellgate train trestle. We usually listen to music out of a boom box and its usually old obscure music from the sixtees and seventees. Most responses are posative however rarely there might be a complaint from people who think that they are in a library. We are old school astoria. A throwback to the way cats hung out in the sevetees when music was shared, experienced together almost like a religious experience. Back then there would be people hanging out all along what was once called the strip along shore road listening to music out of boom boxes. we carry on that tradition. It has taken me a long time to use this medium becuase admittedly i am resistant to this overwhelming assault of technology which in our opinion is diluting humanity itself. Where people once socialized face to face in person now is through electronic gadgets. Admitedly i am finding myself increasingly isolated becuase of my reluctance to accept the changes taking place. But ther are a few of us old timers left in Astoria. In fact i am working on a series of graphic novels about the neighborhood and the guys i hang out with. The stories include most Astortia landmarks and life today from the perspective of us cats in our fourtees and fiftees. Anyhow i thank all who acknowledge this and i am glad to be a part of something that i hope others can relate to.


Peace to all


Fane

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: NYC Native on August 14, 2009, 10:25:32 PM
H E L L O!
I'm Luis F Martinez - aka Lou or Louis as most people call me.  I'm an environmental consultant turned contractor.  I'm also a RE broker.  I do work in the area.  I resisted doing more business in Astoria in the past - I actually found Jackson Hts character more rooted and stable.  The more time I found myself in Astoria I realize that it was truly a dynamic place to do business.  I'm originally from the Bronx and raised in PR but now live in Holliswood.  I find myself practically in Jackson Hts, Astoria and adjacent areas on a daily basis.  I just signed lease and will be opening a small store front in the area.  I hear that Astorians are meaner, haters, immature and love to hide behind their keyboards when they talk trash...heh (I Love it!) - I think that's a byproduct of being young.  Is it me or there's see a big gap in the age groups?  I see lots of bright beautiful young people, working hard making ends meet - paying their rents - looking at the future.  Then  I see much older people - home owners, literally retired and semiretired.  Point is - H E L L O!

Actually, I think these people are in the minority, and I don't believe that every native Astorian carries such prejudice and bias.  It's easy to blame everything on "transplants", so they do.  I mean, come on - NYC was built by immigrants.  Everyone - unless you are from one of the indigenous tribes on this island - is a descendant of people who came here from somewhere else. 

To smear and demean these "transplants" as they do is lazy and small minded on their part. And those that hold on to such anger and vitriol will only stay stranded in their fetid bad attitude swamp.  Be happy you're not in there with them.

Can't remember if you're the person who posted the Jake G. photo or if that was someone else. Either way, both made me smile. Thanks for that.

I remember reading someone's post about a desire to have more long term renters because short term renters in the area treat it like it's a hotel or stop on the way to somewhere better. High turnover often goes hand in hand with disrespectful attitudes and behaviors, but- not always. I'm not a native Astorian but like the part of Astoria in which I live. With the exception of the ongoing native vs. nonnative diatribe on community message boards, I have not had any experiences, good or bad, with anyone in the real live world about this subject. To me, that's a good thing because the more hospitable the people are within a given neighborhood, the more cohesive it becomes which will hopefully keep residents here longer, thus diminishing the tenant turnover.
Title: Re: Hi
Post by: kathleenburns on July 25, 2010, 09:05:57 PM
I was   transplanted here 50 years ago, gosh where did those 50 years go.  my children, grandchildren, great-grandchildren are natives.   i've seen a lot of changes in 50 years.  wish we did have a good supermarket, but that was voted down by the natives.  still miss kiddieland, my children would drag me in there.   i use to walk all around here all the time, there was so much too see.  one thing always got a seat on the subway, never had to stand.  i guess it is packed now.   we did go through the crack era that was rough. we had yellow cabs all the time, then they were gone. seems like they are coming back.  they even had a phone at the cab stand and you could for yellow cab if one wasn't there.  we have seen our share of bombings, the big one one on 31st street, which also took our our post office. now it is in the old greek threater,  they showed American movies before that.  we had department stores, they are gone.   really would like a big hard ware store.  people have told me a lot of history of  Astoria over the years.
Title: Re: Hello
Post by: flikchik on July 26, 2010, 11:40:14 AM
Hi and welcome to everyone.........you've all picked a great place to live.  I'm 48, work as a production coordinator  and I'm a 3rd generation Astorian (my grandparents moved her from Italy back in the 1930's).  And I'm so grateful that they did. 

I moved away for a while but ultimately came back home.  My childhood was here, my grandparent's souls are here, my memories continue here.......my heart will forever live here.

To me...we Astorians have the protected encasement of the Triborough and Hellgate bridges, and the lushness of Astoria Park to call our backyard.  If we continue to take care of our Astoria...it will continue to be the place we're proud to call home.

Jenny

Howdy -

I've been living on Ditmars for about 2 years, enjoying the limited number of restaurants and bars I'm familiar with in the area.  Now I'm the new bartender at Hell Gate Social, so I figure I'd better get social and get to know what people, places and things I've been missing out on.

Places I frequent: Martha's Country Bakery, Igloo, Brooklyn Bagels on Ditmars, Watawa, Sweet Afton, Sparrow, Tasty Corner (blueberry pancakes!!)... a little over the beer garden.  Astor Bakery, which recently opened next to Hell Gate, is pretty close to sublime.

Feel free to give me tips on what I've been missing!  On or around Ditmars Blvd. would be a huge plus...otherwise, anything within biking distance from there is fair game.

I'm at Hell Gate Tuesdays, Fridays and Saturdays - if you're in the area, come by and say hello! (Astoria Blvd between 12th and 14th sts...next to the aforementioned new bakery!!)

Thanks guys!

Post by: micphi on August 02, 2010, 09:56:57 AM
Me and my girlfriend just moved to Astoria now that we've transferred colleges to CUNY Baruch. We're originally from Ulster County. We're not "hipsters" and would prefer not to be considered "transplants" as it makes us feel like we were surgically bound to the area. I'm thinking there's probably no way of shedding that label without a serious time investment in the area and community.

We've got another 3 years of school before we can get our CPA's so we'll be around here for at least that long, and hopefully much longer.

If anyone knows of some good places to grab some food, please let me know. I've been stuck in Chain Restaurant Hell for my entire life, and I'd love to savor the local eats.

There are great places all over Astoria, from Neptune Diner on 31Street and Astoria Blvd to Alba's Pizza on Ditmars and 37th Street and great places in between. Sushi, Italian, Thai, Greek, Indian, you name it.  Depends on where you're living.

Title: Re: Hello
Post by: JAC on September 17, 2010, 03:57:12 PM
Hello Astorians-

I've been lurking around reading posts for a while and thought, what the heck, I'll register and post something.
I've lived in Astoria for just about 2 years with my family. I wanted to move here primarily due to the decent elementary schools, somewhat more reasonable rent and the not having  to commute to work from a great distance. Since I don't commute during NYC traditional rush hour, it's a pleasant ride in to Midtown.
So far we like it here and since we have a child in a public school here we feel more connected to the neighborhood and more invested in where the neighborhood goes from here.

Hello!  My name is Rebecca, and I have lived in Astoria for 13 1/2 years.  Wow, time goes by fast!  I'm a stay-at-home mom recently turned baby sign language instructor.  I've always enjoyed hanging out in Astoria -- I believe there's a great night life here and no reason to go into Manhattan every weekend -- but it wasn't until I became a mom and stayed in Astoria almost 24/7 that I really felt like part of the community.  I'm really proud to call Astoria my home.
